# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# etcd Raft Snapshot Too Old on Node Rejoin

## Your Task

An etcd node fails to rejoin a cluster with 'ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable'. Find the Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that (1) define ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable and (2) implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

```json
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created the answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

The `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` error is part of the Raft snapshot availability check mechanism that occurs when an etcd node fails to rejoin a cluster because its local log is too old.

**Key Findings:**

1. **Error Definition**: `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` is defined in the raft library (`go.etcd.io/raft/v3/storage.go`), which etcd depends on.

2. **Critical File**: `server/etcdserver/bootstrap.go` contains the `MemoryStorage()` method (lines 700-712) that creates the raft.MemoryStorage instance. This is the etcd-io/etcd wrapper that provides snapshot availability to the raft library.

3. **Snapshot Availability Check**: During Raft log catch-up when a slow follower (rejoining node) is too far behind:
   - The raft library's `maybeSendSnapshot()` function calls `Storage.Snapshot()`
   - If the snapshot is temporarily unavailable (still being prepared), it returns `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable`
   - Instead of panicking, the leader gracefully retries on the next heartbeat tick

4. **Related Components**:
   - `raftNode` struct in `server/etcdserver/raft.go` uses the MemoryStorage
   - Bootstrap chain: `bootstrapWALFromSnapshot` → `bootstrappedWAL.MemoryStorage()` → `newRaftNode`

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable defined and how is it used during Raft log catch-up when a node tries to rejoin the cluster?\\n\\nHere's the complete picture of `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` and its role in Raft log catch-up:\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Definition\\n\\n`ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` is defined in [`vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/storage.go`](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/r/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/-/blob/vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/storage.go?L36-38):\\n\\n```go\\n// ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable is returned by the Storage interface when the required\\n// snapshot is temporarily unavailable.\\nvar ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable = errors.New(\\\"snapshot is temporarily unavailable\\\")\\n```\\n\\nIt's part of the `go.etcd.io/raft/v3` library (vendored in many repos including Kubernetes and Moby).\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Role in the `Storage` Interface\\n\\nThe [`Storage.Snapshot()`](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/r/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/-/blob/vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/storage.go?L85-89) interface method is contractually expected to return this error when it needs more time to prepare a snapshot:\\n\\n```go\\n// Snapshot returns the most recent snapshot.\\n// If snapshot is temporarily unavailable, it should return ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable,\\n// so raft state machine could know that Storage needs some time to prepare\\n// snapshot and call Snapshot later.\\nSnapshot() (pb.Snapshot, error)\\n```\\n\\nThe `MemoryStorage` implementation doesn't return this error (it always has a snapshot), but real on-disk storage backends (like etcd's `etcdserver`) do \u2014 typically while a snapshot is still being serialized or flushed to disk.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## The Catch-Up Flow\\n\\nWhen a node rejoins the cluster after being down, the leader tries to replicate missing log entries via [`maybeSendAppend`](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/r/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/-/blob/vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/raft.go?L616-660):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *raft) maybeSendAppend(to uint64, sendIfEmpty bool) bool {\\n    pr := r.trk.Progress[to]\\n    prevIndex := pr.Next - 1\\n    prevTerm, err := r.raftLog.term(prevIndex)\\n    if err != nil {\\n        // The log probably got truncated at >= pr.Next, so we can't catch up the\\n        // follower log anymore. Send a snapshot instead.\\n        return r.maybeSendSnapshot(to, pr)\\n    }\\n    // ...\\n    ents, err = r.raftLog.entries(pr.Next, r.maxMsgSize)\\n    if err != nil { // send a snapshot if we failed to get the entries\\n        return r.maybeSendSnapshot(to, pr)\\n    }\\n    // ... send MsgApp normally\\n}\\n```\\n\\nIf the required log entries have been **compacted away** (i.e., the follower is too far behind), both the `term()` and `entries()` calls fail, and execution falls through to [`maybeSendSnapshot`](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/r/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/-/blob/vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/raft.go?L662-689):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *raft) maybeSendSnapshot(to uint64, pr *tracker.Progress) bool {\\n    if !pr.RecentActive {\\n        r.logger.Debugf(\\\"ignore sending snapshot to %x since it is not recently active\\\", to)\\n        return false\\n    }\\n\\n    snapshot, err := r.raftLog.snapshot()\\n    if err != nil {\\n        if err == ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable {\\n            r.logger.Debugf(\\\"%x failed to send snapshot to %x because snapshot is temporarily unavailable\\\", r.id, to)\\n            return false   // \u2190 gracefully back off, no panic\\n        }\\n        panic(err)         // \u2190 all other errors are fatal\\n    }\\n    // ... send MsgSnap\\n    r.send(pb.Message{To: to, Type: pb.MsgSnap, Snapshot: &snapshot})\\n    return true\\n}\\n```\\n\\n[`raftLog.snapshot()`](https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/r/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/-/blob/vendor/go.etcd.io/raft/v3/log.go?L291-296) first checks the in-memory unstable buffer, then delegates to the `Storage` backend:\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (l *raftLog) snapshot() (pb.Snapshot, error) {\\n    if l.unstable.snapshot != nil {\\n        return *l.unstable.snapshot, nil\\n    }\\n    return l.storage.Snapshot()   // \u2190 may return ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable\\n}\\n```\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Summary of the Catch-Up Sequence\\n\\n| Step | What happens |\\n|------|-------------|\\n| 1 | Rejoining node's `pr.Next` is behind the leader's compacted log |\\n| 2 | `maybeSendAppend` fails to fetch entries/term \u2192 calls `maybeSendSnapshot` |\\n| 3 | Leader calls `raftLog.snapshot()` \u2192 `Storage.Snapshot()` |\\n| 4 | If storage isn't ready \u2192 `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` returned |\\n| 5 | `maybeSendSnapshot` logs a debug message and returns `false` (no panic, no send) |\\n| 6 | On the next heartbeat/bcastAppend tick, the leader retries |\\n| 7 | Once the snapshot is ready, `Storage.Snapshot()` succeeds \u2192 leader sends `MsgSnap` to the rejoining node |\\n\\nThe key design point: `ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable` is the **only non-fatal error** from `Storage.Snapshot()`. All other errors cause a panic. This gives storage backends a safe way to signal \\\"not yet\\\" without crashing the Raft state machine.\\n\\n## Sources\\n\\n-
